### Post by CompyTheInsane on 2010-05-10

### Post by ubunterooster on 2010-05-10
35,really how do you do that?

---

### Post by jetsam on 2010-05-10
0x24

For two hex digits, just multiply the first column (The 16's column) by 16 and add the last column (the 1's column. ) Also, a = 10; b = 11; c = 12; d = 13; e = 14; f = 15.

so 0x24 = 2 * 16 + 4 = 36.

---

### Post by CompyTheInsane on 2010-05-10
0x25 = 37
> **ubunterooster said:**
> 35,really how do you do that?
Three ways that I do this:
- Hex counting starting with the last post that had a hex number (not recommended)
- Converting the number to hex using my brain. See Jetsam's post above me. (Takes too much time)
- using Gcalctool to convert the number to hex.

I don't know if the calculator that comes installed on Xubuntu has a built-in hex coverter.

Also: [http://www.parkenet.com/apl/HexDecConverter.html](http://www.parkenet.com/apl/HexDecConverter.html)

### Post by chessnerd on 2010-05-20
Actually, that Java code would just print all of the numbers from 1 to 500 in the same post. You'd want code that makes post after post, but you'd have to find a toolkit or something to use...
```
import ubuntuforums.toolkit.*;

public class Main {
   public static void main(String[] args) {
      // Poster takes a username and password as parameters
      UFPoster poster = new UFPoster("chessnerd", [censored]);
      poster.setThread("Couting to 500 Before Mod Resets!");
      for (int i = 1; i <= 500; i++) {
         poster.post(i);
      }
   }
}
```

If only, if only...

### Post by jetsam on 2010-05-23
1195 != 0 | CPN - GZP = X | MA = 1695

1195 = GZP

1195 - CPN = DPN

DEC2Hex(DPN) = 0xyy

0xyy

### Post by audiomick on 2010-06-01
Ah.(light bulb lights up).
This
[> ]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/*nix")[*nix]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/*nix") (Unix and related) shells, and likewise the [C programming language]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C_%28programming_language%29"), which was designed for Unix (and the syntactic descendants of C[[2]]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hexadecimal#cite_note-1")) use the prefix 0x for numeric constants represented in hex: 0x5A3.
is what I didn't know...

But don't expect me to do hex conversions in my head at this time of night...

57

### Post by CompyTheInsane on 2010-06-01

### Post by jetsam on 2010-06-09
0x8d

You're correct.  Thanks for catching that.

8D = (8 * 16) + 13 
   = 128 + 13
   = 141
